  4. I ordered this shaver from Amazon before its mid-July release and have been using it for a little more than 2 weeks. Today's multiple blade safety razors lift the hair slightly above the opening of the follicle where it is cut then recedes back into place. Because it was lifted upward first before being cut, it actually returns to a position below the skin surface. <br /> <br />The skin provides protection from certain types of harmful bacteria and it is not perfectly smooth. Hair harbors bacteria and so can your razor. Even trace amounts of the ingredients found in shaving foams/gels plus any leftover stubble is a breeding ground for it. Also, most people leave their razors in the bathroom. Need I say more? Shaving with a blade razor abrades the skin. This abrasion, along with hair receding below the follicle opening, provides access for bacteria to exploit; ergo the hygienic justification for the clean and renew system associated with the Braun shaver. <br /> <br />The shaver and its charging/cleaning base are an attractive appliance with a small footprint. The power cord can either be attached to the charging/cleaning base or directly to the shaver itself. The clean and renew cartridge installs easily into the base. Then plug it in, insert the shaver and allow for initial charging. The unit will not begin the cleaning cycle until the blue button on the front of the base is depressed, so it can be charged from the base without cleaning. The cleaning base has sensors that determine what level of cleaning is necessary. No selection is required. The only time that you need to remove the micro-screen shaving head to clean mechanically with the supplied brush is when you are on a trip and away from the cleaning base. One note about the clean and renew cartridges, the CCR2 and the CCR3 are the same. The number indicates how many replacement cartridges are included in the package. The shaver is ergonomically designed to fit well in the hand, is well balanced, and the controls are very simple. <br /> <br />I really appreciate the improved level of hygiene because of the clean and renew system. Not that I had a complexion problem before using the Braun (I didn't) but my skin looks clearer and has better tone than it has in a long time, maybe ever. I am thoroughly pleased with this product.

  16. I don't write many reviews but I really wanted to take a moment to post about this shaver. I've used several electric razors over the years, including Remington, Norelco, and now two Brauns (and probably a couple of others). I can't shave with a blade because I have sensitive skin but an extremely thick, wiry beard. Blades, even the ones with 4 blades and the lubricating strip etc., just tear my skin up and I end up with several days of irritation, discomfort and red bumps. My last Braun, which I purchased quite a few years ago (and it was expensive at the time), was the best razor I'd used to date, but was still noisy and SLOW. It would take me 45 minutes to get a decent shave even with a brand new head and foil, even with the razor plugged in. Plus it didn't hold the razor stubble in the head very well so I ended up with a mess of razor dust all over my shirt. I got this Braun 360 Complete 8985 last Christmas and for the first time, shaving wasn't a chore but was actually very quick, easy and painless! What a relief. Instead of feeling like I was dragging sandpaper over my face for 45 minutes, it felt like wiping butter off, and I could get the smoothest shave I've ever gotten with an electric razor in under 10 minutes. Actually I was able to get an acceptable quick shave in like 6 minutes, but if I took my time it was even better. Other reviewers have already spoken about the excellent cleaning and charging system, which really is excellent though in fact you do need to keep it in one spot without moving it or it will spill. When I travel I simply take the cord with me for charging and clean it with the brush. I'll also point out that after I shave, I pop the foil open and run the razor over a trash can for a few seconds to shake out the hair, then I clean it quickly with the brush before using the charging/cleaning base. Doing this (and generally only using the base after every other shave), one cartridge actually lasts me about 3 months!!Can't complain about that. I love the clever and useful features like the fact that the base will detect when the battery needs to be conditioned and will actually discharge and fully charge it to condition the battery. And I like the fact that the base somehow senses how much of a cleaning it needs. The razor also just informed me this weekend that I need a new foil and cutter head. What a great feature! When it did that I gave it some thought and realized it has been taking me somewhat longer to shave recently, so yeah, it's definitely time. Nothing's perfect but this razor is absolutely worth the price and it's a fantastic product that has made shaving merely a simple inconvenience for me rather than the painful, time-consuming chore it used to be. (Oh, and it does mostly hold the stubble in the head, so no mess on my shirt or bathroom sink.) Thumbs up, five stars.

  54. (A note before I start: A lot of people who panned this in other reviews seem to think that an electric should shave as close as a manual bladed razor. I guess this might be a self-inflicted view created by the electric razor companies' own marketing teams, but it will never be true. A manual blade shave will always be a better cut than an electric razor.) In terms of an electric razor - compared to other electrics - I have had a great experience with this one. I've had Braun and Philips/Norelco electrics in the past and this is the best of them. It gives a good cut, the 'hedge trimmer' in the middle does a decent job on longer hairs on the occasions when I leave it several days between shaves, and despite what some have reported it doesn't seem any louder than any electric bar shaver I've had in the past. (yes its louder than an electric rotary shaver, but those are always quieter due to the type of mechanism). I like the charging base, but to me its a nice-to-have and not really a feature of the razor itself (which is really the important thing after all). The cleaning solution gizmo is also a good idea, but as many other reviewers here have already mentioned it doesn't need to be used as often as the Braun likes to tell you it does. I use mine once a week max, and in between I just slide the cartridge out and reseal it with the plastic cover it comes with to prevent evaporation. The automatic cleaning process is quite loud, but does that really matter? If you only do it once a week or so, just plan on doing it when people aren't trying to sleep. It's like complaining that a coffee maker is loud when brewing a cappuccino, so what? Don't do it if baby is trying to sleep next to it. I do occasionally find that it does miss some longer hairs in the area at the corner of the jawbone right near the ears, but I can remedy that by going over that area a couple of times again at the end of the shave. It doesn't always do this, so I suspect it has something to do with the angle of the razor when I make the first pass over that area which makes the difference. Overall, a very good razor at a reasonable price.

What's not so good? I hope you're sitting down for this bit. First, with all that unimpeachable construction, it's HEAVY. Drop this on your foot, you might be having a leg off. Also, subtracts from your weight allowance if you're a frequent air traveler. Second, it's NOISY - sort of like starting a 12HP snowblower in your bathroom. If you rise early, and your significant other prefers a more relaxed approach to the day, this can lead to an exquisitely vigorous exchange of views in the early hours. Trust me, I know. Third, while it can give a close, fast shave on PARTS of your face, there are other parts - round the corner of a nostril, for example, or on one side of your neck - where it has only two approaches, both of them unsatisfactory. One is to be apparently incapable of trapping and cutting the hair, so that you have to go over and over that part to get a feel something close to what you had in mind. The other - and it's cunning, it does this when you least expect - is to eat a hole in your face. (And guess what? Having blood on your shirt in the morning is still a fashion flub that will make you an object of derision for the whole day. Unless you change, of course...) Fourth, the running time on one charge is only 50 mins. This is fine if you're not going anywhere because you recharge it when you put it back in its \\"station\\", but if you are going to be away from home for more than about 4 days, you have to remember to take the power cord with you AND have the right plug adapter for the country you're visiting. This is nuts - with all that heft in the thing, you would think that you could be away for home for at least 10 days without a recharge. Fifth, it's expensive - not the most expensive, but still not cheap. In the end, I don't think it's good value. Sadder but wiser, I'm going back to Philips.

I wish I had taken Amazon's automatic replacement policy which is offered for consumables. It would have saved me 15%, but I hadn't felt the benefit of the new cutter bar when ordering. Lately, the red light comes on and it's half full. I just unplug it and it returns to giving accurate readings.

  132. I tried several electrics in the past and could never get a shave that was even close to adequate. My dermatologist wanted me to try an electric again, so I decided to spend the bucks and get the best I could find, and hope it worked. After about 3 weeks of practice, I was finally getting a decent shave. If I want to stay fairly smooth, I'd have to do it again in the afternoon sometime, but usually once in the morning is fine. It isn't an instant shave. It takes me a while to get all the stubble growing in the different directions, but I can get there.<br /><br />I either didn't read it or forgot it, but I noticed the other day that the head wasn't swiveling. Then I saw there were two \\"on\\" positions for the razor, plus one for the clipper. It goes: off-> on (w/swivel)-> fix (no swivel)-> clipper. Can't believe I didn't notice that for several months.<br /><br />I love the auto clean but hate the expensive disposable cartridges.<br /><br />I take the foil off after each shave and tap it and the razor lightly on the sink to knock out the hairs before putting it back in the base. Then I hit the clean button about every 3 shaves (or immediately if it registers 'intense' on the base).<br /><br />I decided to refill the cartridges instead of spending $5 or $6 a piece and throwing away the perfectly good plastic cartridge every time.<br /><br />Ingredients in the cleaning solution are: denatured alcohol, limonene, citral.<br /><br />Denatured alcohol is just ethanol (same as liquor) with a poison added to make it undrinkable. Really - a poison. If they denature it, they don't have to pay liquor taxes. The denatured alcohol in U.S. hardware stores is denatured with Methanol (wood alcohol). Methanol is seriously toxic. But I'm not sure that it would be a problem. The razor has a drying cycle that would evaporate both the ethanol and the methanol. Besides - the concentrations we'd contact from the razor and base are very low. \\"Dose is the difference between medicine and poison\\". Get too much of one thing and it can poison you (salt, caffeine, water,...), small doses are usually not a problem for many toxic substances. They use this ethanol methanol mixture as the fuel to heat chafing (keeps food warm) dishes and fondue pots also. I'm really not sure what to think about it.<br /><br />The other ingredients are Limonene and Citral. Limonene is a terpene. Terpenes are great. They get them from plant oils. The most common is d-limonene. It is usually extracted from orange peels and smells wonderful. It works as a solvent in full concentration (a couple of wipes with a paper towel, took some adhesive goo off my kitchen floor that I'd tried to get off with many different cleaners) and a general purpose cleaner when diluted. It even shows up in cosmetics, some foods and is in some hand soaps to add that nice citrus smell, and lots of other places. They can use it to clean factory machines. It's a great degreaser and doesn't release CFC's like the chemical cleaners. It's safer for the staff also.<br /><br />I'm guessing the limonene, besides cleaning away the skin oils, is a lubricant also. It has a bit of an oiliness to it. It adds a great orange citrus smell too. I don't use much. Really only about 1/100th of a cent worth, but I have no idea what the proper amount to use is.<br /><br />I'm also using the denatured alcohol with methanol. I don't know if it's safe yet, so don't trust me on that. The denatured alcohol doesn't smell as nice as the cleaning fluid. They probably use another agent to denature the alcohol in their cleaning fluid. I wish I could get pure ethanol. Maybe I should try Everclear?<br /><br />After the cleaning/drying cycle, the razor smells almost exactly the same as with the purchased cartridges. The citral in the ingredients is a fragrance and I decided - for me - it was probably optional, so I haven't tried to track it down. I bought d-limonene at greenterpene dot com. (d-limonene smells like oranges, l-limonene smellslike turpentine - I'm pretty sure they use the d-limonene).<br /><br />I rinse the cartridge with a little alcohol to get the hair out - I don't use water - because water can corrode metal. Then I fill it with about $1.25 worth of the alcohol and a tiny amount of limonene. The cartridge holds 175ml-it's on the label. I had a full one and just scratched a line on the side so I'd know how much to add. Seems to be working well for me, but I really can't recommend it as I don't know about the methanol issue. I'll let you know if my ears fall off. Or if the razor has problems.<br /><br />I wouldn't use drugstore Isopropyl alcohol (rubbing alcohol). It has water, acetone, methyl isobutyl ketone, denatonium benzoate - a bittering agent, sometimes fragrance and coloring agents, plus other stuff - there are different recipes depending on the manufacturer. I'm afraid of all those extra ingredients harming the razor.<br /><br />Well, that's my recipe. I really can't recommend it though until I find out about the methanol issue, although I like it. If someone finds a pure ethyl alcohol that is denatured with something milder, let me know. Thanks.<br /><br />And I do love the razor.he cartridge with a little alcohol to get the hair out - I don't use water - because water can corrode metal. This selection is likely based purely on time in use, and you can't step back. That is, you can't select \\"eco\\" if the shaver recommends \\"normal\\" (short of hitting the Reset button on the shaver, I suppose).<br /><br />In any case, no big deal, as I am a couple weeks over one month and my original cartridge is still in place. (Users in dryer climates may see quicker replacement intervals as the alcohol-based cleaning fluid readily evaporates).<br /><br />Lastly, travel is a pleasure! As others have mentioned, the base unit stays at home, and the cord plugs directly into the shaver. The hard travel case and screen protector are both welcome features as I have had shavers power on while stashed in my luggage.<br /><br />All-in-all, I wished for a slightly closer shave with this Braun, but I'm pretty pleased with my purchase.<br /><br />Edit (10/2/06): Short hairs on my neck have turned out to be more problematic with this shaver than my old Panasonic.<br /><br />As I indicated in my original write-up, I am now convinced I received a closer shave along the jaw from the Braun 8585 I used briefly before purchasing this 8985 360° complete model. I don't know if it's due to the change to the new Gillette cutter block, or if it's luck of the draw, but with the 8985 it's definitely an increased investment in time (by a few minutes) to shave each morning.n use, and you can't step back. Although Braun today is not the same company or designs of yesteryear. Nevertheless, despite being a Philishave user for all the years prior to last week, I definitely have a new-found prejudice toward the Braun shaver name. But I dug out my two old Philips shaver models, and started to compare them to the Braun 8975. The first is the Philips 4821, and the other is a more higher end but even older (1990?) Philishave 955. I stopped using the 955 years ago, because the 4821 appeared to have a stronger motor and shave better.<br /><br />Well, my more careful recent tests have shown me that the 955 is actually better than the newer 4821. This may well be why the heavier Braun 8975 appears to shave closer than the lighter 590cc. But, I found the Philishave 955 superior to the Braun 8975. With the 955, in no time I could get a shave on any part of my face, that was so close that you felt no stubble at all when brushing up with your hand. So-called \\"baby's bottom\\" smooth (the shave was just a touch rougher on the skin than the Braun 8975 or 950cc). Since that is the ultimate that you can expect from a shave, no matter which method you use, I have to give the Philips 955 a 5-star rating. I think the fact that you can shave in circles with the rotary shavers gives it an advantage over the foil type. That action seems to catch and pull the skin better, that can result in a closer shave.<br /><br />Note, the 955 is an old shaver that must be around 23 years old (I have NEVER changed its shaving heads), does not have the latest foil or technology buzzwords, does not have the latest \\"3D\\" flexi-head design, does not shave wet, does not even have NiMh batteries, is probably worth $10 on the used market today, yet it shaves better than the $400 Braun 8985 and every other Braun or Philips shaver I've tried. And it costs you 0 cents per year in cleaning station fluids. So DONT BUY BUZZWORDS. Sure, you can say electric shaver technology has advanced over the years --but that does not mean it has progressed! Of course, this finding is all very disappointing to me, because I wanted to stick with a Braun shaver! What I might do is just keep my old classic design Braun 5561 out in the open in my bathroom, for decoration. Then hide the Philips 955 in a cabinet somewhere for when I actually want to shave!

Moreover, it's faster and without any mess.<br /><br />It should be noted that face should be dry prior to shaving, or else shave will not be nearly as close. All in all, it's a great product in terms of performance, reliability and comfort.
  216. I have two shavers, an older Norelco 8160XL and a new Braun 8985. The Norelco provides a much closer shave and shaving time therefore shorter. The shaving head in the Braun is more flexible, which gives the Braun a slight edge on surfaces of your skin that are not even. However the Norelco is more sturdy and does not bend away when you try to shave an area. Thus on your cheeks and most of the neck the Norelco does a better job. I have to replace the Norelco's blades about every 12 months. The Braun states that blades should be replaced every 18 month, so this seems to give the Braun a slight edge. The cleaning station is nice, but has one big disadvantage. If you put the shaver in the cleaning station it gets hot. So if you have to shave an area again because the shaver did a lousy job and you did not realize that, then you have to do it with a hot shaver. Overall I am less then happy with the product. The shaver comes with a 60 day return policy. So keep the package and you can return the product to Braun.

  219. I bought this shaver/clean & renew charging base used off Ebay for $37.09 plus $10.00 shipping for a total of $47.09, so I wasn't expecting much. My expectations, however, were far surpassed once I took delivery of this fine piece of German engineering. It was in perfect, near-new condition, and after an overnight charge, it lept into action and aggressively attacked my two-day growth of facial hair. I had used the Gillette Sensor twin blade system for the last 15 years. I shaved with it in the shower using shaving oil. Irrefutably, this produced a good, clean, and close shave, but it also scraped away a microscopic layer of skin each day. Now that I have celebrated my 52nd birthday, my skin seems thinner and more prone to trauma, and blade shaving began to take its toll. In addition, the oil that I used with the blade began to make a mess that I had to clean from my shower stall, and I knew that I was spending more time in the shower--wasting hot water--than I would if I could find a good electric, dry shaving alternative. I began a several-month quest to gather research in hopes of bypassing all the substandard models of shavers out there. The Braun Pulsonic was top-rated, but I seriously couldn't see paying some $200 for this product. I also found that the Remington MicroScreen 500 MS2-390 was highly-rated, but I liked the idea of Braun's clean and renew system. A July 2008 Consumer Reports article that rated Braun's 8985 model its #1 choice put me over the top, and I decided that the 8985 would also be my choice. I was patient in my quest to find the best possible deal, and then a couple weeks ago, BAM! I submitted the winning $47.09 bid for an 8985 Braun shaver on Ebay. I've shaved with this unit for a full week now, and I must report that, \\"No, it does not shave as close as a blade.\\" I doubt that this holy grail of shaving will ever be achieved with an electric shaver, at least in my lifetime. However, it does shave surprisingly close,and it does the job quickly. Indeed it takes me no longer to shave with the electric that it used to with the blade. In addition, I will now save hundreds of gallons of hot water (and a lot of money) each year by shaving in front of a mirror instead of in the shower. Indeed, I'd say that my showers are now approximately 33% shorter in durration. Of course, I did have to learn to contort my face, hold and stretch my skin with my off-hand, and run the razor in just the right direction against the grain of hair growth on all parts of my beard. After a week of this, though, I now have it down-pat, and I have to say that the shave I get is \\"good enough.\\" I understand that a shavee must allow up to a couple months of acclimation in order to receive the closest possible shave, so I anticipate that the closeness of my shave will only get better from here. The Clean & Renew system works well too. After reading several posts, though, I've decided to only use it on a weekly basis, and in hindsight, I doubt that anyone would have to use it more often than that. I do remove the screen every other day and gently tap out the clippings. Also, I plan to look into making my own formula to refill the clean and renew cartridges (the ingredients appear to consist mostly of SD Alcohol 40-B which, I found, is made nondrinkable not by making it poisonous, but by making it extremely bitter). Thus, this type of alcohol can be exposed to the skin without any risk of being poisoned via absorption through the skin. Sorry, I got off the main topic. I must leave you with \\"Two Thumbs Up\\" for the fine Braun 8985 Shaver. It just feels substantial and durable, and when I am shaving, it doesn't even bog down the motor. This is worlds ahead of the last electric shaver I used back in the mid-80s (a Panasonic). I know I'll be enjoying the 8985 for a long time to come.

  239. I have been using Braun shavers for 20 years or so. I like them better than any other electrics I have tried. This one does an adequate job of shaving. My big problem is the base. On my old 7000 series, the base allowed my to set it to clean or charge or both. This one just has a button to start the cleaning cycle but it charges every time. This presumably will shorten the life of the battery because you are charging it more often than you need to. Also, it has a sensor that shows the level of fluid left in the cartridge, something I just checked manually on the old shaver base. The problem is when this one senses the level is too low, it will not continue to do a cleaning cycle until it gets a new cartridge. At the point where it forces you to change cartridges, there is still about 2 weeks worth of fluid left. Consequently, over the life of this shaver (and my last one lasted 5+ years) this one feature will cost you hundreds in extra refills. Not to mention all the wasted chemicals and plastic from those extra refills. Sure, Braun makes a lot more money off you. Good for them in the short term. Bad for them in long term customer satisfaction. If they don't address this, I will probably start looking for another brand.

  273. I hesitated paying the sticker price for the Consumer Reports top rated Braun 8985 360. I have used electric razors for over 50 years including Remington, Norelco, Krups, Braun and some others. The very inexpensive Braun I was currently using was not satisfactory because it seemed to take forever to get only a passable shave. The Braun 8985 360 lists at about $170 and includes an automatic cleaning and recharging system that I was unconvinced I really needed, however, its performance was rated excellent and so it has proved to be. I am able to get an excellent, close shave amazingly fast compared to my inexpensive model. In fact, the Braun 8985 outperforms any electric razor I have ever used. The automatic cleaning and recharging system is recommended after each use, however, I use the system only once per week substituting hand cleaning the rest of the week and that has worked out fine. Altogether superb shaver.

  279. This is a decent enough shaver, but doesn't live up to the sales hype. I got a fairly good deal on mine at CostCo, but it was still pretty expensive. I figured at that price, and with the Braun name behind it, it would be worth it. Lots of talk about close shaves, no tugging, etc.<br /><br />I found that it does tug and pull at the whiskers, and the shave is not all that close. Perhaps compared to other electric shavers it is, but I find that I have to go over my beard again and again to get all the whiskers, and by the time I come close to getting them all, I am likely to create some minor abrasions. Sometimes, entire patches seem to resist the shaver, despite my best efforts, leaving an uneven look.<br /><br />If a whisker happens to get missed by the shaver a couple times and grows too long, it will not be shaved in the future at all, and will continue to grow until you happen to notice that you've got a ridiculous looking \\"old man whisker\\" growing out of your neck.<br /><br />The replacement cartridges for the cleaning fluid are expensive too (although despite what Braun says, you CAN refill them with denatured alcohol for pennies). The replacement foil and cutter block are also expensive, so the cost of ownership is outrageous as well.<br /><br />The Clean and Renew station takes up a lot of counter space, and is not well built. My stopped working, so I went online to look at a replacement, and read everyone's review which said the same thing. That it is fragile and impossible not to have it stop performing all its functions in time.<br /><br />This unit appears to be more of a device for Braun to sell replacement parts and refills than anything else.<br /><br />The quality of the shave is acceptable, but nothing more than that. It is useful for if I want to multitask and shave while watching TV or sitting on the throne. But honestly, if I had a mulligan, I would never buy this, and probably wouldn't get an electric shaver at all. The rising cost of quality razors drove me to consider this, but the cost of razors is nothing compared to the ownership cost of this shaver. A traditional shave in the shower, using shaving cream and a quality razor, is quicker, more comfortable, and in the end, cheaper as well.quality razors drove me to consider this, but the cost of razors is nothing compared to the ownership cost of this shaver.
